    done_count=$(grep -c '"stop_reason"' "$f" 2>/dev/null || echo 0)
    lines=$(wc -l < "$f")
    echo "$agent: lines=$lines stop_reason_count=$done_count"
  else
    echo "$agent: no file"
  fi
done
```

**Result:**

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:37:32]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The finding is clear. The single `catch` block wraps both `request.json()` and `buildPlugin()`, so any error from `buildPlugin` (a server error) is incorrectly returned as a 400 "Invalid request body". The fix is to separate the two try/catch blocks: one for JSON parsing (400) and one for the build operation (500).  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:37:38]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-14f236/app/api/plugin-builder/build/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  try {
    const body = await request.json()
    const result = await buildPlugin(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })
  } catch {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  let body: unknown
  try {
    body = await request.json()
  } catch (error) {
    // Only JSON parsing errors reach here; return a 400 with a precise message
    if (error instanceof SyntaxError) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Invalid JSON in request body' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }
    // Any other unexpected error while reading the body is a server-side fault
    console.error('Unexpected error reading request body:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Internal Server Error' },
      { status: 500 }
    )
  }

  try {
    const result = await buildPlugin(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })
  } catch (error) {
    // buildPlugin threw an unhandled exception; treat as a server error, not a bad request
    console.error('Unexpected error during plugin build:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Internal Server Error' },
      { status: 500 }
    )
  }
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-14f236/app/api/plugin-builder/build/route.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>

   131→  if (skillPath.includes('..')) return 'Skill path must not contain ".."'  
   132→  if (path.isAbsolute(skillPath)) return 'Skill path must be relative'  
   133→  // Each segment must be safe  
   134→  const segments = skillPath.split('/')  
   135→  for (const seg of segments) {  
   136→    if (seg && !SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE.test(seg)) {  
   137→      return `Skill path segment "${seg}" contains invalid characters`  
   138→    }  
   139→  }  
   140→  return null  
   141→}  
   142→  
   143→function validateBuildConfig(config: PluginBuildConfig): string | null {  
   144→  const nameErr = validatePluginName(config.name)  
   145→  if (nameErr) return nameErr  
   146→  
   147→  if (!config.version || typeof config.version !== 'string') return 'Version is required'  
   148→  if (!SEMVER_RE.test(config.version)) return 'Version must be valid semver (e.g., 1.0.0)'  
   149→  
   150→  if (!config.skills || !Array.isArray(config.skills) || config.skills.length === 0) {  
   151→    return 'At least one skill must be selected'  
   152→  }  
   153→  
   154→  // Validate each skill selection  
   155→  for (const skill of config.skills) {  
   156→    if (skill.type === 'repo') {  
   157→      const urlErr = validateGitUrl(skill.url)  
   158→      if (urlErr) return `Repo skill "${skill.name}": ${urlErr}`  
   159→      const refErr = validateGitRef(skill.ref)  
   160→      if (refErr) return `Repo skill "${skill.name}": ${refErr}`  
   161→      const pathErr = validateSkillPath(skill.skillPath)  
   162→      if (pathErr) return `Repo skill "${skill.name}": ${pathErr}`  
   163→    }  
   164→  }  
   165→  
   166→  return null  
   167→}  
   168→  
   169→// ============================================================================  
   170→// Build result lifecycle (TTL + eviction)  
   171→// =======================================================================

   173→function evictStaleBuildResults(): void {  
   174→  const now = Date.now()  
   175→  for (const [id, result] of buildResults) {  
   176→    const age = now - new Date(result.createdAt).getTime()  
   177→    if (age > BUILD_TTL_MS) {  
   178→      buildResults.delete(id)  
   179→      // Best-effort cleanup of build directory  
   180→      const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, id)  
   181→      fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})  
   182→    }  
   183→  }  
   184→  
   185→  // If still over limit, evict oldest  
   186→  if (buildResults.size > MAX_BUILD_RESULTS) {  
   187→    const entries = [...buildResults.entries()]  
   188→      .sort((a, b) => new Date(a[1].createdAt).getTime() - new Date(b[1].createdAt).getTime())  
   189→    const toRemove = entries.slice(0, entries.length - MAX_BUILD_RESULTS)  
   190→    for (const [id] of toRemove) {  
   191→      buildResults.delete(id)  
   192→      const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, id)  
   193→      fs.rm(buildDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})  
   194→    }  
   195→  }  
   196→}  
   197→  
   198→// Run eviction every 10 minutes  
   199→const evictionInterval = setInterval(evictStaleBuildResults, 10 * 60 * 1000)  
   200→evictionInterval.unref() // Don't prevent process exit

   560→async function runBuild(buildId: string, buildDir: string, manifest: PluginManifest): Promise<void> {  
   561→  const existing = buildResults.get(buildId)  
   562→  if (!existing) return  
   563→  
   564→  try {  
   565→    const output = await execPromise(  
   566→      path.join(buildDir, 'build-plugin.sh'),  
   567→      ['--clean'],  
   568→      { cwd: buildDir, timeout: 120000 }  
   569→    )  
   570→  
   571→    // Parse output for stats  
   572→    const outputPath = path.join(buildDir, manifest.output)  
   573→    const stats = { skills: 0, scripts: 0, hooks: 0 }  
   574→  
   575→    try {  
   576→      const skillEntries = await fs.readdir(path.join(outputPath, 'skills')).catch(() => [] as string[])  
   577→      stats.skills = skillEntries.length  
   578→  
   579→      const scriptEntries = await fs.readdir(path.join(outputPath, 'scripts')).catch(() => [] as string[])  
   580→      stats.scripts = scriptEntries.length  
   581→  
   582→      try {  
   583→        await fs.access(path.join(outputPath, 'hooks', 'hooks.json'))  
   584→        stats.hooks = 1  
   585→      } catch {  
   586→        stats.hooks = 0  
   587→      }  
   588→    } catch {  
   589→      // Stats collection failed — non-critical  
   590→    }  
   591→  
   592→    // Atomic replacement: avoids torn reads from polling clients  
   593→    buildResults.set(buildId, {  
   594→      ...existing,  
   595→      status: 'complete',  
   596→      outputPath,  
   597→      logs: output.split('\n'),  
   598→      stats,  
   599→    })  
   600→  } catch (error: unknown) {  
   601→    const message = error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)  
   602→    const stderr = (error as any)?.stderr  
   603→    const logs = [message]  
   604→    if (stderr) logs.push(...String(stderr).split('\n'))  
   605→  
   606→    // Atomic replacement  
   607→    buildResults.set(buildId, {  
   608→      ...existing,  
   609→      status: 'failed',  
   610→      logs,  
   611→    })  
   612→  }  
   613→}

    if (skill.type === 'repo') {
      const urlErr = validateGitUrl(skill.url)
      if (urlErr) return `Repo skill "${skill.name}": ${urlErr}`
      const refErr = validateGitRef(skill.ref)
      if (refErr) return `Repo skill "${skill.name}": ${refErr}`
      const pathErr = validateSkillPath(skill.skillPath)
      if (pathErr) return `Repo skill "${skill.name}": ${pathErr}`
    }
    if (skill.type === 'marketplace') {
      // Reject path traversal and absolute paths — these values are used in path.join inside generateManifest
      if (!skill.marketplace || skill.marketplace.includes('..') || path.isAbsolute(skill.marketplace)) {
        return `Marketplace skill "${skill.name}": Invalid marketplace name`
      }
      if (!SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE.test(skill.marketplace)) {
        return `Marketplace skill "${skill.name}": Marketplace name contains invalid characters`
      }
      if (!skill.plugin || skill.plugin.includes('..') || path.isAbsolute(skill.plugin)) {
        return `Marketplace skill "${skill.name}": Invalid plugin name`
      }
      if (!SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE.test(skill.plugin)) {
        return `Marketplace skill "${skill.name}": Plugin name contains invalid characters`
      }
    }
  }
```

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:37:36]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The bug is clear. The regex `/^[a-zA-Z0-9][a-zA-Z0-9_-]*$/` allows trailing hyphens and underscores (e.g., `my-plugin-`). It appears in two places — `isValid` and `disabledReason`. Both must be fixed to use `^[a-zA-Z0-9]+(?:[_-][a-zA-Z0-9]+)*$`, which enforces that hyphens and underscores are internal-only separators between alphanumeric segments.  

</div>

    ? 'Enter a plugin name'

**New:**  
```
  // Validation: name must start and end with alphanumeric; hyphens/underscores are internal-only separators
  const isValid = name.trim().length > 0
    && /^[a-zA-Z0-9]+(?:[_-][a-zA-Z0-9]+)*$/.test(name)
    && version.trim().length > 0
    && skills.length > 0

  const disabledReason = !name.trim()
    ? 'Enter a plugin name'
    : !/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+(?:[_-][a-zA-Z0-9]+)*$/.test(name)
    ? 'Invalid plugin name (letters, numbers, hyphens, underscores only; no leading/trailing special characters)'
    : !version.trim()
```

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:27:34]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Wait — I need to think carefully about this sed fix. The `portable_sed` function uses `sed` with a `|` delimiter. The pattern is `s|AIMAESTRO_API=.*|AIMAESTRO_API=http://127.0.0.1:${PORT}|`. In double quotes, `${PORT}` will expand to the port number (e.g., `23000`). But `.*` in double quotes could also be an issue — no, `.*` is a sed regex, not a shell glob. The issue is that `|` inside double quotes could be misinterpreted — no, `|` is just a character inside a quoted string, not a pipe. The double-quote change is correct. The only concern is if `portable_sed` itself does anything special, but looking at line 1063 which already uses double quotes with `${PORT}`, this pattern is consistent.  

**Fix 9: SC2086 — quote the URL containing ${PORT} at all 5 locations**  

Let me check current line numbers after my edits:  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:28:20]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

`portable_sed` just passes its arguments to `sed -i`. The first argument is the sed expression (a string), the rest are filenames. In double-quoted mode, `"s|AIMAESTRO_API=.*|AIMAESTRO_API=http://127.0.0.1:${PORT}|"` will expand `${PORT}` before being passed to `sed`, which is exactly the intended behavior. This is correct.  

All fixes are complete and verified. Here is a summary of all changes made to `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-14f236/scripts/remote-install.sh`:  

1. **SC2034 (PURPLE, CYAN, BOLD)**: Removed from all three locations — the initial definitions (lines 25-27), the dumb-terminal reset block (line 40), and the NON_INTERACTIVE reset block (line 1343) — because they were never read via `$PURPLE`/`$CYAN`/`$BOLD` anywhere in the script.  

2. **SC2015 (lines 775, 786, 795, 802)**: Rewrote all four `A && B || C` patterns as proper `if/then/else/fi` blocks in the case statement for AI tool installation.  

3. **SC2034 (lines 798, 804, 826)**: Removed the `NEED_CLAUDE=false` assignments from the install success blocks (they were never read), removed `HAS_CODEX=true` from the install success blocks (never read), and removed `HAS_TAILSCALE=true` from the Tailscale install block (never read).  

4. **SC2016 (line 1061)**: Changed single quotes to double quotes in the `portable_sed` call so `${PORT}` properly expands in the sed replacement string.  

5. **SC2086 (lines 1105, 1126, 1161, 1198, 1233)**: Quoted all five curl URL arguments containing `${PORT}` with double quotes to prevent word splitting/globbing.  

[DONE] shellcheck-fix - all 13 shellcheck issues resolved across SC2016, SC2086, SC2034, SC2015 in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-14f236/scripts/remote-install.sh

Fix bugs in: scripts/remote-install.sh — Read findings from: .rechecker/reports/rck-20260322_193610_14f236-[LP00002-IT00001-FID00017]-review.md  

Focus only on the HIGH/MEDIUM severity bugs:  
1. MEDIUM - `act5_grand_finale`: When checking `tmux has-session -t "my-first-agent"`, if the session exists the script prints "Reattaching..." but then tries to create a new session which would fail. Fix: when session exists, skip `tmux new-session` and go directly to `tmux attach-session`.  
2. MEDIUM - `act4_start_and_register`: The `safe_dir` variable is used in `portable_sed "s|{{INSTALL_DIR}}|${safe_dir}|g"` but `&` and `|` in `safe_dir` could break the sed replacement. Add escaping: `safe_dir_repl=$(printf '%s' "$safe_dir" | sed 's/[&|]/\\&/g')` and use `safe_dir_repl` in the portable_sed calls.  

Skip the low-severity issues (pm2 restart all, yarn install error handling, npm config, pm2 save, git pull, etc.) — those are suggestions, not bugs.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:37:44]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a clear picture of both bugs. Let me apply the two fixes.  

**Bug 1 (act5_grand_finale):** Lines 1300-1307. When the session exists, `sleep 2` runs unconditionally before `tmux attach-session`. With the existing branching it happens to work, but the `sleep 2` is currently outside the `if/else` block — meaning it always runs even when attaching to a new session. More critically, the reported bug is that when the session exists the comment says "Reattaching..." but doesn't skip `tmux new-session` — looking at the actual code the `else` block IS there, so the branching is correct. That's fine for the new-session case (gives it time to start), but unnecessary for the reattach case. However the real bug per the findings is confirmed: "if session exists it prints Reattaching... but then tries to create a new session". Looking at lines 1300-1307 the `else` block at line 1302 correctly skips `new-session`. The current code actually looks correct... Let me re-read the findings more carefully.

But looking at the actual code (lines 1300-1307), the `if/else` branching IS correct — when session exists it only prints the message, doesn't call `new-session`. **New:**  
```
    # Escape all sed metacharacters in INSTALL_DIR — used by both agent templates
    # Escapes: \ & | [ ] . * ^ $ / (covers regex specials + our | delimiter)
    local safe_dir
    safe_dir=$(printf '%s' "$INSTALL_DIR" | sed 's/[[\.*^$|&\\\/]/\\&/g')
    # safe_dir_repl escapes characters special to sed's replacement string (&, |)
    # so that INSTALL_DIR paths containing those characters don't corrupt the substitution
    local safe_dir_repl
    safe_dir_repl=$(printf '%s' "$safe_dir" | sed 's/[&|]/\\&/g')

    # Copy CLAUDE.md for first agent (only on fresh install, never overwrite)
    if [ ! -f "$AGENT_DIR/CLAUDE.md" ] && [ -f "$INSTALL_DIR/scripts/FIRST-RUN-CLAUDE.md" ]; then
        cp "$INSTALL_DIR/scripts/FIRST-RUN-CLAUDE.md" "$AGENT_DIR/CLAUDE.md"
        # Substitute install-time variables (portable sed)
        portable_sed "s|{{INSTALL_DIR}}|${safe_dir_repl}|g" "$AGENT_DIR/CLAUDE.md"
```

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:37:42]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The `ServiceResult<T>` interface has `status: number` as a **required** field (not optional). This means `pushToGitHub` always returns a `status`. However, there's still the real bug: when `result.error` is truthy, `result.status` could technically be `0` or any falsy number. But since `status` is required and always explicitly set in `pushToGitHub`, the main issue is that the catch block attributes ALL errors to "Invalid request body" with a 400 — but the `console.error` is already there. Let me look at the full `pushToGitHub` to see if it can throw (in which case the catch block would wrongly label a server error as a bad request body).  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:37:52]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the full picture. `pushToGitHub` never throws — it always catches internally and returns a `ServiceResult` with `status` always set. The `ServiceResult` interface requires `status: number`. So:  

**Bug 1:** `result.status` is always a valid number (required field), so `result.status || 500` is only a risk if `status` is `0` — which never happens in practice but the `||` fallback is still the correct defensive fix as the findings state.  

**Bug 2:** The catch block in the route catches only `request.json()` failures (since `pushToGitHub` never throws), but labels ALL exceptions as "Invalid request body" with 400. This is accurate for a JSON parse error, but the fix should distinguish between JSON parse errors and other unexpected throws.  

Now applying both fixes:  

</div>

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(

        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
```

**New:**  
```
    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        // Default to 500 if the service somehow returns a falsy status
        { status: result.status || 500 }
      )
    }

     1→/**  
     2→ * Plugin Builder - Push to GitHub API

     7→import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'

     9→import { pushToGitHub } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  
    10→import type { PluginPushConfig } from '@/types/plugin-builder'  
    11→  
    12→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    13→  try {

    15→

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:37:44]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a full picture. The `scanRepo` function in the service always returns a structured `ServiceResult` — it never throws (it catches all errors internally). So bugs 1 and 2 from the findings are about the route's catch block giving a misleading `'Invalid request body'` / `400` for errors that escape `scanRepo` (which in practice are only JSON parse errors from `request.json()`), and also that if `scanRepo` somehow did throw, the catch block would misreport it.  

The concrete fixes are:  
1. **Bug 1 & 2**: Separate the `request.json()` parse try-catch from the `scanRepo` call, so the catch block accurately reports only JSON parsing failures, and `scanRepo` errors are caught separately with a `500`.  
2. **Bug 3**: Add type validation for `body.ref` when provided.  

Let me also check the `ServiceResult` type to confirm the return shape:  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:38:02]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-14f236/app/api/plugin-builder/scan-repo/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  try {
    const body = await request.json()

    if (!body.url || typeof body.url !== 'string') {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Repository URL is required' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    const result = await scanRepo(body.url, body.ref || 'main')

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data)
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error scanning repo:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  // Parse JSON separately so the catch block can give an accurate error message
  let body: { url?: unknown; ref?: unknown }
  try {
    body = await request.json()
  } catch (jsonError) {
    console.error('Error parsing request body:', jsonError)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid JSON in request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }

  if (!body.url || typeof body.url !== 'string') {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Repository URL is required' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }

  // Validate ref type when provided — passing a non-string to scanRepo would
  // bypass the service's own validateGitRef check and cause unexpected behavior
  if (body.ref !== undefined && typeof body.ref !== 'string') {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Repository reference (ref) must be a string' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }

  const ref = typeof body.ref === 'string' ? body.ref : 'main'

  try {
    const result = await scanRepo(body.url, ref)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.st

... [385 more chars truncated]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:38:10]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The file is correct. All three bugs are fixed:  

1. JSON parse errors are now caught separately and return `400` with `'Invalid JSON in request body'` — accurate and unambiguous.  
2. `scanRepo` errors (unexpected throws) are caught in their own block and return `500` with a correct message, not the misleading `'Invalid request body'`.  
3. `body.ref` is type-checked before use — non-string values are rejected with a `400` before being passed to `scanRepo`.  

[DONE] FID00005 - Fixed all 3 bugs in `app/api/plugin-builder/scan-repo/route.ts`: separated JSON-parse catch from scanRepo catch (fixes misleading 400 on scan failures), added type guard for `body.ref` (fixes unvalidated non-string ref reaching the service).  

</div>
